Spring and Autumn

Not Thorough 207

— Sisou

China's thousands of years of history can be described as a completely not thorough history. No matter which aspect, it is not thorough. Just like changing dynasties, which is considered the biggest change in history; however, besides changing surnames, what thorough change has there been? I am afraid that only the murder of the descendants of the previous dynasty is the most thorough when changing surnames. The Song, Qi, Liang, and Chen of the Six Dynasties were only thorough changes in terms of changing surnames and killing the previous imperial family. There was no sign of change even on the surface. Most of the high-ranking officials of the previous dynasty maintained their original positions. And Feng Dao of the Five Dynasties actually served four dynasties and thirteen monarchs, and held the positions of generals and ministers. He was very proud and called himself the "Old Man of Lasting Joy." The changes in the dynasties after the Song and Yuan Dynasties only replaced another group of people in the court, and society was still the old society, with no changes at all. Unfortunately, the Xinhai Revolution repeated the same mistakes. It only transferred power from the hands of the Manchus to the hands of the Northern Warlords. The revolutionaries could not even stand in their homeland in an instant. Society remained the same, and the people were struggling to survive, with a sigh of things getting worse! How terrible is this "not thorough" malady!

Unexpectedly, China's lack of thoroughness has even been transmitted to foreigners in the concessions! When we walk on the road, we often encounter a black car, the compartment is rectangular, and it is as big as a room. The front and rear doors are closed and driving. It is a car specially used to catch petty thieves. There are Chinese and Western police officers on it, patrolling on the roads. When they see petty thieves, they stop and catch them, saying it is for the sake of tidying up the city. But after being caught and sent to the police station, they are only detained for two or three days and then released. After being released, they still obstruct the city, so they are caught again, released again. After being released, they are still caught, without end.

In fact, this lack of thoroughness is not only limited to foreigners in the concessions. Looking at the international arena, what kind of meetings, what kind of agreements, are all not thorough? However, the wheel of time will eventually move forward; there will eventually be a day when "not thorough" will be shattered, and there will be a thorough great thoroughness.

Airplane and Armored Vehicle 208

— Lanxi

Speaking of these two terrible and hateful weapons, we will associate with the panic situation during the Shanghai War last year. Overhead, there were airplanes circling with squeaking sounds, and in the distance, there were armored vehicles attacking. These were all sent by the enemies. Under the terror of these airplanes and armored vehicles, we in Shanghai at that time were really frightened.

And now Nanjing is also greatly suffering from the same terror. (Please readers be patient and listen to me quietly) According to Mr. Chen, who often goes to Nanjing on official business, the number of airplanes and armored vehicles in Nanjing is so large that you cannot count them. The residents of Nanjing are very worried because there are too many of them. Everyone has to suffer from the attack of airplanes and armored vehicles. The people of Nanjing compare mosquitoes to airplanes and bedbugs to armored vehicles.

It is also fortunate that they can think of it. These two small animals are really like the two weapons mentioned above. Airplanes squeak, mosquitoes buzz, and the same is circling over your head, and when there is a chance, they will nail you for a while (just like bombs under the plane), so that on your good flesh, there will be a little bit of red and itchy scars. (This is the area after the bomb falls) After the mosquito stings you, it flies away satisfied. It also works like an airplane. And the stupid armored vehicle is just like a bedbug. Slow progress, bulky body, but it is not easy to kill it. It cannot be drowned or starved to death. It nails when it sees meat, causing it to bulge, and it is poisonous and not easy to eliminate.

From this, we can see the degree of terror that the people of Nanjing have for mosquitoes and bedbugs. They actually compare them to these two weapons. As a joke, if all the mosquitoes and bedbugs in China were transformed into airplanes and armored vehicles, then China's strength could be expected in the near future, and the authority of the Great Republic of China would not only be deeply feared by the "bandit country," but also be the hero of the world. Because Mr. Chen told me this, I was filled with emotion, so I described it as above.

Preferential Treatment for Prisoners 209

— Baihe

It seems that two years ago, a White Russian vagrant in Shanghai, because he could not find bread, had a whimsical idea and broke the large glass on a shop window with a punch. After being sentenced to detention, he was very happy, because he could get temporary food, clothing, and shelter without cost. He said that after serving his sentence and being released, he would still use this method to solve his livelihood problem. Although the next time has not been resolved, "being sued" is one way to make a living, which is indeed the safest.

We have seen in recent years that prisons in various places are like large hotels in Shanghai, often with "full" signs hanging. At first, I thought that the public security personnel were serious in their work and miraculously solved cases, so there were so many prisoners. But after thinking carefully, it is not right. Among these prisoners, there must be countless "friends who eat for free" living in it. The country spends so much on prisoner rations every year, but it is used to supply these street bums who are not within the thirty-six lines and take being sued as a temporary occupation. It is really unjust.

A few days ago, someone accused a certain prison of deducting prisoner rations, and I was sweating in my palms, because once the prisoner rations were not deducted, the prisoners would be full. Although prisons are not a good place, friends who have no food to eat will not run to soup kitchens, but regard prisons as shelters. That would be terrible.

These days, it's even worse. I heard that prisoners get a national sexual release once after a considerable period of time. There is also a rumor that the interrogation of prisoners will be strictly prohibited. If it becomes a reality, then, of course, there will be no "slaps" when entering the door, let alone spanking or electric shocks. After entering prison, there is prisoner rations to eat, which can fill your belly, and you don't have to worry about being cold or hungry. Being full and warm, you can also go home for sex. Isn't it better than being away from home and not being able to get enough to eat?

If preferential treatment for prisoners is implemented, "friends who eat for free" will definitely feel at home. I don't know if the authorities have ten thousand mansions to accommodate them. If there is not enough time to rush to build prisons to accommodate them, then, I think it is better to have an exam, and only those who pass will be allowed to enter prison to enjoy food, clothing, and shelter, in order to show restrictions, which may be feasible.

A Few Foreign Fanatics 210

— Chaoye

At the beginning of this summer, I accidentally received a special income. According to my wife's original intention, it was to be deposited in the bank for emergencies. In my opinion, it is better to buy a practical item than to keep it in the bank. When bright people come and go, I can use it to pretend to be decent, and also make a few familiar friends confused and in awe and envy. As a result, I bought a timely Huasheng desk fan. One day, the wife of my relative who studied in England deigned to visit me. After exchanging greetings, she first turned on the electric fan to show preferential treatment. Unexpectedly, the wife smiled and stopped it. I was terrified and killed the electricity. My wife asked suspiciously, "Is Mrs. So-and-so not hot?" The wife replied arrogantly, "I came by car, the sun can't reach me. This kind of Chinese electric fan is very noisy, I really can't get used to it. I have always used 'Emerson'."

The wife of a certain classmate who has not stepped out of the country's gate is particularly interested in "foreign" things. She doesn't wear yellow leather shoes that are not imported, and she must buy socks from the Shanghai Huiluo Company. There are really few domestic goods in the home, and the most incomprehensible thing is that she must eat Western food in summer. Because there are no authentic Western restaurants in Nanjing, she actually eats every day at the home of a certain Westerner in a certain oil company, and the monthly fee is slightly equal to the income of a first-class staff member. One day, a certain couple came to my residence. Because it was close to lunch time, my wife and I insisted on them having a meal. The wife said with a sad face, "We were originally going to have lunch at Mrs. Hutchinson's house, but because it was a little early, we came to your place to rest our feet. Besides, I never eat Chinese food in summer." After listening respectfully, I couldn't help but feel angry. In a hurry, I blurted out, "Then the dishes made by Mrs……'s family are all authentic imports?" The wife did not answer, but the classmate said "goodbye".

A friend of mine dined at my place one day. After the meal, we chatted. Later, he saw my gramophone, stood up, opened the box, and searched for records for a long time. I asked strangely, "Which one are you looking for?" He said, "I'm looking for 'Home is Home'." I had never heard of this record title before, and I didn't like listening to foreign records at all. Actually, I really couldn't understand it, so I apologized for not having it. The friend shrugged his shoulders, turned his palms, and laughed, saying, "Chinese records are for country bumpkins to listen to."

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 211

Chapter 14: It is difficult to get married, and I am worried about the future. Inviting friends to a small gathering to remember the past with embarrassment.

After a while, I only heard someone shouting outside the house: I brought a guest, who is the host, I am sorry. Zhao Ziqiang did not consider it and replied loudly: Miss Huang is willing to come, I am the host. Before he finished speaking, the curtain was lifted, and Huang Manying pulled someone in. It was not someone else, but Yang Guizhi. This was beyond Zhao Ziqiang's expectation. He was stunned and didn't know what to do. Guizhi's body was stiff when she lifted the curtain, and she wanted to run backwards. She turned around and glared at Huang Manying and said: Didn't you say there were no outsiders? As for who is an outsider and who is not an outsider, we don't have to argue about it. This time, Zhao Ziqiang was really stiff. Should he entertain them well, or should he not entertain them? He coughed lightly twice and tugged at his clothes, and then said to Manying: Miss Huang, what would you like to order? Originally, they were sitting at a long table. Zhao Ziqiang sat at the head of the table, Tian Qing sat on his left, and Manying Guizhi sat on his right. When he spoke to Manying, he could also say that he was talking to Guizhi. Manying said: I want to eat a bowl of yuanxiao. Miss Yang, what would you like to eat? When she said this, she first looked at Zhao Ziqiang, and then turned her head to smile at Guizhi. Guizhi thought to herself, if I answer shyly, they will say that I am stingy, so she straightened her chest and smiled slightly: I will also eat a bowl of yuanxiao. Huang Manying and Tian Qing applauded in unison. (177)

Woman's Paradise

Lantern Melon 212

(1) The Fun of Lantern Competitions Ten years ago, in my childhood, I always liked to play with many children of similar ages! The playing methods were different because of the different seasons!

Making melon lanterns was not very popular because the weather was very hot, and we often liked to tell stories with many older sisters, younger sisters, older brothers, and younger brothers in summer nights; so, it was not very popular; when the weather got a little cooler, we would make many melon lanterns with many children, and go out in groups to compete with lanterns when the night god came!

Many children's hands were holding melon lanterns, which were arranged very neatly in front and back, which was very beautiful! Sometimes, everyone would walk and sing; the spirit of unity can be expressed here. Who says that the Chinese are like a plate of loose sand?

(2) How to Make a Melon Lantern

Whether it is a big watermelon or a small golden melon; the best is a kind called Banggua in Shanghai and Western watermelon in the countryside to make melon lanterns!

During the day, when eating watermelon, do not cut a watermelon into two halves; naturally! To make a melon lantern, you must make a watermelon shell like a beautiful lamp; so, when eating watermelon during the day, you only need to cut off a part of a watermelon at the end where the watermelon flower falls off, like a small basin, and then take out the heart inside with a spoon and eat it; scrape the inedible inner skin thinly to make it like a lamp shell, this is the first step! The second step is to make two wide and thin small bamboo strips into a cross shape and put them in the middle of the melon, but at the intersection of the two bamboo strips, you need to use a thin thread to make a pointed head for inserting candles!

Secondly, after cutting off a spoon-shaped piece, you need to evenly punch four holes on the edge, which is to tie four thin hemp threads to hang on a small bamboo pole!

Finally, light a candle inside the melon lantern, and you can hold the lamp in your hand and run around to play!

For more particular ones, many calligraphy and paintings are carved around the melon lantern, such as a double happiness, or the three characters of Fulu Shou, or the four characters of Tianxia Weigong, or other characters, or other painted scenes, etc.!

If the words and paintings of resisting Japan and saving the country are carved on the lamp, then it is more full of patriotic thoughts!

The Golden Cage of the Spinning Lady 213

— Ye Yi

At the turn of summer and autumn, under the poplar trees or pumpkin leaves, there are many spinning ladies chirping at night; many families without gardens can go outside to catch a few spinning ladies to raise at home; but, where to raise them? The following are several ways to raise them:

1. Bamboo cage is made of fine bamboo silk; its shape and texture are the same as ordinary bird cages, but smaller! This kind of cage can be bought or made easily. Just use twelve thicker small bamboo sticks, about two inches long, to set up a square frame, and then drill many small holes on the bamboo sticks, and insert many fine bamboo silks! But it is a little troublesome to make

2. Lead wire cage is woven from many fine lead wires. As long as there is a place where a spinning lady can enter, it can be raised!

3. Leaf wire cage is woven from large bamboo leaves, and the method is the same as the lead wire cage! Just weave many thin bamboo threads vertically and horizontally, make six sides in total, and then sew them together with thin thread, and open a small door, and it's done!

4. Melon shell Use a small melon shell, cut off a little bit of the top, and then dig out the inside heart, and punch a few small holes thinly on the shell, and it becomes a golden cage for the spinning lady!

However, after the cage is made, what should the spinning lady eat? That is to pick a few pumpkin flowers and small edamame (soybeans) for it to eat in the morning, and it will be fine!

Page 16

Published every Sunday, Issue 38

The Problem of Flooding in Collapsing Rural Areas 214

— Zong Fan

Human survival is the result of constant struggle against nature. Agriculture, entirely a product of nature, has an even deeper relationship with it, and the struggle with nature is therefore particularly close.

China is a country that has based itself on agriculture for five thousand years. Its land is fertile and its products are abundant. This is not only something we have always been proud of, but our entire nation relies on this endowment to be well-fed and clothed, and to live a life of ease and leisure. But how did the land become so fertile? How can the products be so abundant? What we get from heaven is limited; the efforts and struggles of our ancestors account for the largest and most important part. If we open the history of any era and examine the industry of any place, all dikes, ditches, and even the construction of rivers, and the opening up of agricultural reclamation, have undergone decades or even hundreds of years of hard work before there can be considerable harvests. Otherwise, the vast wilderness is just barren land!

However, now, China's entire agriculture is collapsing. Not only are all farmers on the verge of starvation, but even the raw materials for the clothes we wear, such as cotton and cotton yarn, are imported from foreign countries at a value of two to three hundred million taels each year; the food we need every day, such as rice, wheat, and flour, are also imported at a value of two to three hundred million taels each year. Moreover, these imports are constant, long-term, and increasing year by year. The collapse of agriculture has led to a sharp increase in foreign imports, and this influx of imports has made it even more impossible for China's agriculture to be revived! This cycle continues until the entire Chinese nation perishes!

The reason for the collapse of China's rural areas and the massive import of foreign necessities is naturally very complex, but the Chinese government's failure to build water conservancy projects, and the exploitation of Chinese farmers at every level, leaving them unable to restore or resist natural disasters such as floods and droughts, can be said to be the most important reason. Moreover, it can also be said that the increasing severity of floods everywhere in China can be used to measure the deepening degree of the collapse of Chinese agriculture.

The great flood along the Yangtze River in the 20th year of the Republic of China affected sixteen provinces. According to the investigation by the Flood Relief Committee, the losses from the more severe disasters in only seven provinces – Anhui, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Henan – showed that the area actually affected by the flood and reported accounted for 32.5% of the total area; the flooded farmland reached 127,706,452 mu; the property loss was estimated at 1,575,330,360 yuan; and the number of disaster victims was 43,300,849, accounting for 25.9% of the total population of the above counties. (The above statistics are all based on the 1933 Shen Bao Yearbook, pages P70-71) The severity of the losses from this great flood can of course be said to be unprecedented. It not only affected the national economy and people's livelihood, but also the occurrence of the Manchurian Incident by Japanese imperialism was directly or indirectly foreshadowed or triggered by this great flood. As for last year, according to the investigation, it was the year with the lightest disasters in the past five years; however, the floods in Jilin, Heilongjiang, Shanxi, Yunnan, and other provinces, the various disasters of floods, droughts, wind, hail, and black frost in Shaanxi, the breaches of various rivers in Hebei, and the combination of floods followed by droughts in Jiangxi, also affected as many as seven provinces. Moreover, because of the impact of the great flood in the previous year, the rice-producing provinces encountered a bumper harvest, but the price of grain was very low, and the suffering of the farmers was even more severe than in the year of the disaster!

As for this year, fortunately, the danger of the Yangtze River in June and July barely passed; however, recently, due to the breach of the Yellow River, more than one hundred counties in Henan, Shandong, Hebei, Shaanxi, Jiangsu, and Anhui provinces were affected; (August 30th Chen Bao) The breach of the river embankment in Hua County, Henan Province, submerged more than 6,000 square li, totaling more than 600 villages; (September 1st Shen Bao) The floods in Xiangxiang County, Changde, Lingling, Huarong, and other counties in Hunan Province submerged 300,000 to 400,000 mu of farmland (July 22nd Chen Bao). In the past two months alone, there have been records in the newspapers almost every day. It is estimated that as many as sixteen provinces have been affected by the disaster, and the number of victims has reached 100 million (August 17th Shi Shi Xin Bao). Although the amount of loss is not as huge as that in the 20th year of the Republic of China, it is definitely not small!

Mallory said that between 108 BC and 1911 AD, China had 1,828 famines. In other words, every year, at least one of China's eighteen provinces had a famine. If we compare his statistics with the current situation, we don't know how much the expansion of the famine has differed. Moreover, the examples he cited included all disasters such as floods, droughts, wars, bandits, wind, frost, and insect pests in China. Zhu Kezhen, in his "Climatic Changes in China Since Historical Times," published statistics on floods and droughts that occurred every hundred years from the early Tang Dynasty to the early 20th century. In particular, floods were most frequent during the Yuan and Qing dynasties; but this is naturally incomparable to recent years, and we can know the obvious relationship between politics and disaster here.

Since the Republic of China, famines have been more frequent and widespread. The Huai River flooded in 1913, submerging 10,470 square miles in Anhui and 2,300 square miles in Jiangsu; the great flood in Jiangxi in 1924 turned hundreds of square miles of fertile land near Ganzhou into a swamp; along the Yellow River, 80,000 square miles of land were submerged in 1925; in 1927, the provinces in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River were flooded by tens of thousands of square miles. These tragic stories are all in our latest memories. In this famine-stricken China, the disaster of 1931 will inevitably expand even more. Although the great flood of 1931 has passed, the disaster of 1933 is coming. And the disasters in the future will only become more and more intense; the periodic law of labor pains will become shorter and shorter! China's agriculture, which has been painstakingly built for thousands of years, will inevitably be completely destroyed in a few years, and the entire Chinese nation will inevitably collapse completely with this flood!

We have already said that the arrival of this flood is a manifestation of the collapse of China's rural areas; and the collapse of rural areas is the cause of this flood. Therefore, if we want to save our own nation, we must first revive China's rural areas, and at the same time, we must restore water conservancy and works related to water conservancy. In conclusion, if we want to survive, we should fight against nature; as for the necessary items that must be prepared before fighting against nature, we should naturally actively prepare for them, and this goes without saying.

Water Conservancy and Floods 215

— He Bing

㈠ The Role of Water Conservancy in the Economy

Varga believed that without water conservancy in China, there would be no agriculture. Ma Jia's research on China's rural economy also focused on the role of water conservancy in the economy. The distribution of the natural environment in the provinces of mainland China can be roughly divided into two major regions, namely the Loess Plateau and the Paddy Field Region. Loess is distributed in Hebei, Shanxi, northern Shaanxi, Gansu, and the northern and southern counties of Shandong and Henan. These areas are historical treasures of China. Loess is a soil that has been soaked by rivers for a long time and accumulated and precipitated. It can absorb rainwater. This water, in the deepest place, encounters the wet air in the lowest layer of the soil, which is rich in nutrients. Through capillary action, it rises to the surface and brings all the nutrients from the bottom of the earth to the surface. Therefore, loess itself can be used as fertilizer, and the soil is often very fertile. However, these advantages of loess must have sufficient water to be expressed. Without sufficient water, the capillary action that occurs on the surface and underground will stop, and plants will not get nutrients. Precious loess will become a barren land.

The southern paddy field area naturally needs even more water. The main plant in the paddy field area is rice. The characteristics of rice, as Professor Copeland said, "Rice needs nourishment and respiration just like other plants. If you want to promote the realization of this essential process, there must be water... If the water supply in those places is very complete, then the growth of rice does not need rain. But in addition to insufficient water, rice is sometimes damaged by too much water..." Therefore, in China, water conservancy is undoubtedly a factor that determines the prosperity or decline of agriculture. On the one hand, it needs water, and on the other hand, it prevents too much water.

In China, water conservancy almost occurred at the same time as agriculture. After the Spring and Autumn Period, irrigation methods gradually became popular. The Historical Records of Rivers and Canals states: "Ximen Bao diverted the Zhang River to irrigate Ye, in order to enrich the area within the He River of Wei." This is not without reason. For example, the strength of Qin was due to the opening of the Zheng Guo Canal.

Today, the abundance and decline, high and low prices of agricultural products and land in China are largely determined by water conservancy. In the Weibei Plain area of Shaanxi, "It is said that in the past, the opening of the Zheng Guo Canal turned barren land into fertile land, and Guanzhong has never had a bad year since then. Later generations continued, and the rise and fall of water conservancy led to the prosperity and decline of land productivity and products" (quoted from "China Rural Economic Materials," page 763). In most parts of Suiyuan Province, "the growth of crops almost entirely depends on the irrigation of rivers and canals. Because irrigation can increase yields and ensure a harvest, land prices are also very different?" (ibid., page 1149).

㈡ Blessed Water

In the relationship where water conservancy determines most of agricultural production, water is naturally blessable for ordinary farmers. Farmers often cherish water more than expected. For example, in Sichuan, there are many good paddy fields that are only cultivated for one season, and are left idle in winter. The reason is the lack of water. As Dong Shijin's investigation showed, "After the rice harvest in Sichuan, if the water is drained and dry crops are planted, it is feared that there will be a shortage of water in the fields in the spring of the following year, and seedlings cannot be transplanted. The loss will be great, so it is impossible not to store water in advance from autumn. This is the biggest reason why farmers dare not grow dry crops in winter" (ibid., page 821).

Since water is so precious, struggles for water are inevitable. For example, in Hunan Province, "Due to the drought this year, farmers often fight and even litigate for water... There is no fixed standard for the time of water rotation. Those who are strong and powerful often take too much" (ibid., page 1113). In Shanxi, the water distribution system is very impressive. The water flowing through a village is owned by that village. "The method of using water is stipulated according to the village and the period. Some use ten days as a period, or half a month as a period... The customs of Zhaocheng and Yuci counties are relatively fierce. Often, villages downstream and villages upstream fight for water, and there are often murder cases" (ibid., page 755). Storms of fighting for water and preventing floods occur everywhere. For example, as reported in the Da Wan Bao in June last year and the Shi Shi Xin Bao on July 5, farmers in Xiaoxian County, Jiangsu, and Suxian County, Anhui, even had a fight of two to three thousand people for water. The Chen Bao Xin Ye Bao on July 11 this year had the following record of the water dispute in Shanxi Province:

"Villagers in Nanhongdong, Zhaocheng, and other counties often fight each other for water to irrigate their fields in the summer, causing disputes and fights. Many villagers on both sides have died under wooden, iron, and firearms... Since the beginning of summer this year, various counties have suffered from drought, resulting in residents of Beiying and Pingquan villages in Qingyuan County engaging in a fierce fight on the 6th and 7th of last month (June) over water for irrigation. Pingquan Village, with its large population and strength, used a repeating rifle to kill one villager from Beiying Village, and seventeen people were lightly or seriously injured."

㈢ Water Conservancy Construction

Although Chinese farmers need water so urgently, small farmers are unable to carry out large-scale irrigation systems. Water conservancy construction is a social undertaking. Farmers who cultivate a few mu or even dozens of mu of land not only do not have the ability, but also cannot build a water conservancy system themselves. Therefore, water conservancy construction can only be expected from the central and local governments.

In Chinese history, one of the important responsibilities of so-called good central governments or local upright officials was to build water conservancy. Only by building water conservancy can they gain the support of the people. During the Han Dynasty, "Shao Fu Du Mu" is still praised as a good story. As the Later Han Dynasty Book records:

"During the reign of Emperor Yuan, Shao Xin Chen was the governor of Nanyang. Sixty miles south of Rang County, he built the Qianlu Pool... to expand irrigation. It increased year by year, reaching 30,000 qing. The people benefited from it. Later, Du Shi, as governor of the Later Han, restored his business. At that time, people sang: There was Shao Fu before, and Du Mu after."

The custom of farmers worshiping water conservancy builders still exists today. Professor Bai Lang was very surprised when he investigated rural Sichuan: "The creators of this kind of large irrigation system are respected by farmers as gods, and are worshiped with solemn ceremonies. The rules for supplying water have also become a major religious ritual for the people of the area, and the canals are cleaned once a year" ("Materials," page 859).

Because of the importance of water conservancy to agriculture, governments of all dynasties attached special importance to it and established special officials to manage it. Special rewards were given to local officials who made contributions to water conservancy construction. The rapid growth of the Chinese nation can be said to be directly proportional to water conservancy construction. In the past, when Westerners came to China and saw the greatness of our country's water conservancy construction, they all sighed and praised it. For example, Li Shufen, after seeing the convenience and regulations of China's irrigation facilities, sighed at it as a miracle of mankind and recorded it. For example, the original dikes of the Yellow River, the water networks in the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River and the Pearl River were all agricultural facilities rarely seen in various countries around the world.

㈣ "Water Disaster"

Agriculture's relationship with water is two-sided. On the one hand, it needs water for irrigation, and on the other hand, it needs to prevent water damage. Therefore, water conservancy construction has two aspects: one is to popularize the irrigation system, and the other is to prevent flood damage. In other words, water is blessable ("happy water") within the appropriate degree, but it can also become a curse ("disaster water") at the wrong time.

Since water conservancy construction cannot be undertaken by individual farmers, it must rely on the government. Therefore, the clarity of politics is directly proportional to the construction of water conservancy, and political changes can affect the changes in water conservancy. Ouyang Xiu recorded the relationship between the opening of ditches and politics in the Geography of the Tang Book:

"Generally speaking, those before the Tianbao era accounted for seven tenths. Isn't it because in the era of peace, official governance was repaired and the people's concealment was revealed, so officials often created benefits for thousands of years? As for after the use of troops in Hebei, the priority was to urge the payment of taxes, and there was no time to study agricultural work and waterways?"

Molay, in his book "The Nile and Egyptian Civilization," also quoted Napoleon as saying: If the national administration is good, the river channels will be repaired, the river tides will be regulated fairly, and the irrigation will benefit many people; if the administration is bad, corrupt, and weak, the river channels will be silted up, the dikes will not be repaired, and not only will they not benefit, but they will also overflow and cause endless harm.

The frequent occurrence of floods in China today has its origins.

First, after the Republic of China, it cannot be said that there are no special officials for water management, but they are equivalent to being set up in vain. On the active side, the irrigation system cannot be popularized, and on the passive side, the dikes cannot be built to prevent water. Although there is a slight amount of water conservancy funding, the result is just to create some corrupt historical facts. Not to mention the causes of the Yangtze River flood in the 19th year, there is also news about the Yellow River breach today:

"The Shen Bao reported on August 28 this year: "The dike funds in Hubei Province have not been cleared for several years, and encroachment and misappropriation are regarded as commonplace. The occurrence of the flood in the previous year completely revealed this secret... Long-term negligence led to repeated cases of encroachment and misappropriation. In addition to Mao Zhongcai, the supervisor of Changyueguan... who encroached and misappropriated dike funds and fled without a trace... secondly... and other cases, the amount of deficit was relatively large. County magistrates, directors of finance bureaus, and directors of collection bureaus in various counties, who defaulted on or misappropriated donations, amounted to more than ten thousand..."

Second, construction is impossible, but there is more than enough destruction. The most powerful thing to destroy water conservancy is war, and wars have been constant in China in recent years. Not to mention the unintentional destruction in the war, there are also many who use water as a means of attack and defense. The Shi Shi Xin Bao reported on May 23 this year:

"Liu Wenhui's troops occupied Chongning on the 17th, and Huang Yin's troops retreated to Guanxian, breaching the dikes and defending to the death. More than a dozen counties along the river were flooded, and crops were submerged, which is worrying for agricultural affairs.

"Liu Wenhui issued a second order on the 19th to launch a general attack on Deng's army. The battles in Jinmacheng Qinggangshu in Guanxian were fierce. Liu failed to cross the river and ordered the Jiangdeng Weir to be destroyed to reduce the water flow of the Pi River, but the water in the outer river rose, and all counties along the river were affected by the water..."

Third, not only that, but sometimes, even "disaster relief" is impossible. The Shen Bao reported on August 28 this year with a notable message, that is, the telegram from the disaster victims in 18 counties in western Shandong said:

"...Since the breach of the long dike in Hebei, we are deeply worried about the flood entering Shandong, and people are panicked and shocked several times a day, but the breach was caused by bandits, who do not care about national law. Hearing this, we are excited and helpless. It is not unique, but more and more strange. The Henan Provincial Government openly sent a brigade of troops to Landui to breach the dike and flood the area. The Landui River dike was breached that night, and the flood flowed horizontally, pouring into western Shandong... a dozen counties and the Cao Ning area..."

These are not accidental or exceptional "examples," but are they universal phenomena?

Highways and Water Conservancy 216

— Duan Sheng

"Rather than building more highways, why not invest more in water conservancy?" This has been a recent argument made by some. I believe that it reflects an understanding of the vital importance of water conservancy. In my opinion, our nation's road infrastructure has been neglected for too long, leading to poor transportation and inconveniences, which has hindered cultural, industrial, and commercial development. Especially with the advancement of military tactics and sophisticated weaponry, the use of heavy artillery, supply trains, and offensive vehicles relies on extensive and direct roads. Therefore, highway construction is essential for national defense and pacification efforts and cannot be delayed. However, those who advocate for water conservancy have their own perspectives, arising not just from the recent Yangtze River floods and Yellow River overflows, nor from opposition to highway construction, but from considerations of the nation's economy and people's livelihoods. They argue:

(1) Considering Agriculture and Food Supply

Agriculture thrives when there is timely rain and sunshine, ensuring smooth development and bountiful harvests. If this is not the case, it is hoped that there are ways to regulate droughts and floods to minimize crop losses. While timely rain and sunshine are gifts of nature beyond human control, droughts and floods, though natural occurrences, can be mitigated through human efforts. Developing water conservancy and dredging rivers and canals can prevent floods, alleviate waterlogging during prolonged rains, and mitigate droughts. Due to the lack of water conservancy in our country, rivers and canals cannot contain floodwaters, leading to overflows. Prolonged rains cause water accumulation and submersion. In times of drought, the earth cracks, and crops wither due to lack of irrigation. "Easy to flood when it rains, easy to drought during dry spells" is the most profound suffering of Chinese agriculture and the reason why food supply is often insecure. Therefore, if China wants to revitalize rural areas and solve the food problem, there is nothing more urgent than water conservancy. Water conservancy benefits both transportation and agriculture. Prosperous agriculture leads to affluent farmers, affluent farmers lead to a stable society, a solid national foundation, and a solution to the food problem.

Furthermore, highway construction can potentially harm rural areas. While providing convenience for national construction, highway routes may disrupt rivers and harbors, and divide land and fields. If handled properly, with the construction of culverts and bridges, farmland can still be irrigated. However, to save costs, farmland water conservancy is often disregarded. Land that has been requisitioned is promised compensation, but payment is delayed indefinitely. Even after land has been requisitioned, farmers are not exempted from land taxes and must still bear the obligation to pay taxes. While this is due to the misconduct of contractors, it is unrelated to the highways themselves. However, instead of causing grievances among the people, why not allocate some of the funds for highway construction to water conservancy, so that farmers sing praises like in the days of Emperors Yao and Shun?

(2) Considering the Needs of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce

It is generally believed that completed highways facilitate traffic, transportation, and travel, boosting industry, commerce, and agriculture. However, reality may not meet expectations. (1) Taking agriculture as an example, although Shanghai and its surrounding areas have a network of roads, agricultural products are not transported by vehicles as much as expected. The reason is that highways often pass through remote villages and towns, reducing their utility. (2) From the perspective of industry and commerce, besides transportation, the benefits of highways are no different for farmers. How many freight transport businesses operate on the completed highways, and how is their business? Do industries and businesses along the highways use vehicles, especially automobiles, for transportation? While this argument may be biased towards the South, even in the North, where carts and horses are common, few have the financial means to use automobiles for transportation. Given this situation across the North and South, the utility of highways, apart from military transportation and political communication, is limited to a few people "enjoying leisure on their days off" or facilitating travel for those with more wealth.

(3) Considering Plugging Loopholes

In recent years, the export of domestic goods has declined, while the import of foreign goods has penetrated every corner of the country. The trade deficit increases year by year, leading to rural bankruptcy and economic hardship. Highway construction promotes the sale of foreign goods. This statement may seem alarmist, but it is true. From the tools used for road construction to automobiles, from screws and nails to engines, generators, axles, tires, and decorative materials like paint, wood, and glass, almost everything is foreign-made. The construction of a highway and the use of automobiles create business for foreign factories and commissions for foreign companies. No wonder foreigners praise China's highway construction as a sign of civilization and progress. The biggest drain is gasoline. Cars cannot run without gas, and gas is consumed as it is used. Over time, the consumption is astonishing. The price war among British, American, and Russian oil companies shows the bright future of oil, and the competition will intensify. Although the price drop benefits us temporarily, it will ultimately cause endless harm. In contrast, water conservancy, river dredging, and boating, though slow, have no such drains. Even the use of steamboats is not comparable to the dependence on foreign goods of automobiles. Therefore, the greatest loss from highway construction and automobile use is the reliance on imported materials, vehicles, and gasoline. The more highways built, the bigger the drain. In today's economy, we should conserve foreign goods and use domestic goods. How can we build highways without considering the harm?

(4) Considering Highway Usage

Recent highways are often poorly built due to cost-cutting and haste. They are rough and uneven, causing vehicles to shake, making them prone to damage and requiring costly maintenance. They primarily serve passengers and not freight, offering little benefit to agriculture, industry, and commerce. In the North, where carts and horses are common, highway construction is a convenient adaptation. However, in the South, with its many ports and rivers, where boats have traditionally been the mode of transportation, building highways while neglecting water conservancy is unwise.

The above are the arguments of those who advocate for water conservancy over highway construction. I believe that highway construction should proceed with the progress of the times without hesitation. However, with the country facing crises and disasters, rural bankruptcy, empty households, and people in dire straits, it is crucial to prioritize the people's livelihood. Every effort should be made to conserve the nation's vitality and reduce waste. All construction should be based on the needs of the majority, the urgency, the social situation, and the global trends. While highways and automobiles are useful for transportation and are common in Europe and America, promoting highways to embrace Western civilization, improve China's road infrastructure, and develop agriculture, industry, and commerce is not objectionable. However, can China's industries, customs, and circumstances be the same as those in Europe and America? If not, we should embrace the trends while considering our social situation. If we must build more highways as the foundation of construction, we should strive for self-sufficiency in vehicles, materials, and gasoline. Otherwise, even with highways as dense as spiderwebs, money will continue to flow to Southeast Asia, Europe, and America.

Deep Disaster! 217

— He

Amidst the soaring rhetoric of the "Rural Revitalization Movement," as a portion of the fifty million U.S. dollar cotton and wheat loan is about to be allocated for rural revitalization, the Yellow River, as if descending from the heavens, rages from Hebei, Henan, Shandong, and Jiangsu, its momentum no less than the Yangtze River flood of 1931. The flood victims, already numbering three million, exceed twice the number of industrial laborers who constitute China's labor problem.

This year can be described as a "nation beset by numerous disasters." Starting in June, the Yangtze River began to swell, once even surging onto the banks, with water several feet deep in the Hankou area. Fortunately, it did not continue to rise as in 1931, but the danger was imminent. At the same time, various counties in Shanxi also reported floods, while in various counties in Shaanxi, "rats are larger than cats." In the Xuhai region of Jiangsu, "locusts swarmed through." Combined with the Yellow River breaching its banks, the affected counties not yet included, the following areas have suffered disasters:

(1) Hunan Province: Floods and droughts

(2) Henan Province: Floods, droughts, hail, frost, wind, locusts, etc.

(3) Shaanxi Province: Droughts, frost, wind, hail, ice, epidemics, etc.

(4) Hubei Province: Floods and droughts

(5) Anhui Province: Wind, floods, and hail

(6) Gansu Province: Droughts, epidemics, and earthquakes

(7) Zhejiang Province: Floods

(8) Jiangxi Province: Floods

(9) Hebei Province: Floods

(10) Guizhou Province: Droughts, hail, and floods

(11) Fujian Province: Droughts, floods, and wind

(12) Sichuan Province: Floods

(13) Jiangsu Province: Floods and locusts

(14) Qinghai Province: Droughts

These are still considered "minor disasters" that, in the past, would have been recorded in history books, with emperors issuing edicts "blaming themselves." But since the Republic, they have become commonplace. However, the Yellow River breach in July, which is now raging and inundating Hebei, Shanxi, Henan, and Shandong, extending to Jiangsu, creating three to four million victims, is a serious event even in today's disaster-stricken times.

In the past, just as ancient Egyptian civilization relied on the Nile River for development, the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers contributed significantly to the rapid growth and development of the Chinese nation. But today, the Yangtze River floods annually, becoming a "scourge" for the central region's residents. And now, the Yellow River has become a true "Yellow Peril." In reality, it's not just the Yellow River; every river beneficial to our lives can suddenly turn into a scourge.

The characteristic of civilized people is the ability to overcome the harms of nature and utilize natural resources, but the Chinese people of the 20th century have reverted to the lives of the prehistoric era. Famines occur every year, and flood prevention, disaster relief, and rescue have become old tunes. Disaster prevention is not difficult, but it is also the most difficult. The Yellow River water conservancy projects, once famous in history and admired by foreigners, are now completely destroyed! While the water conservancy projects are constantly destroyed, we hope that disaster prevention and flood control measures can be effective. The key lies in whether the political system can get back on track.

The disaster is deep! The people are suffering! Relief efforts for the river disaster are still in their initial stages. In the past three days, eight typhoons have hit the coastal areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, all rice and cotton-producing regions. The extent of the damage is still unknown. If the damage is severe, it will add insult to injury, and rural recovery will be even more distant. It is hoped that the authorities will pay close attention to this.

Bond Market: Government Bonds Still Brewing Last Week 220

丨Sudden Rises and Falls, Minor Fluctuations丨

During the week of August 28th to September 2nd, the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange remained lackluster. Although the September futures contracts have been settled and the October contracts have been launched, and Finance Minister Song has returned home with accolades, and there are rumors of restructuring of the 96 bonds, the trading volume has not improved, and the prices have not changed. The increasing rebellions in Fujian province have dampened the spirits. The market has been hovering and brewing for almost a month. With such a long period of dormancy, any change in the environment will cause a rapid and significant price fluctuation. Therefore, both investors and speculators are extremely cautious, making the market even more sluggish. The results of the Lushan Conference will have a significant impact on the market. On Monday, only the September contracts were traded. Due to Finance Minister Song's return, the market showed some activity, but with sudden rises and falls, the trend was still inconsistent, and prices only slightly improved by 0.2-0.3 yuan. On Tuesday, October futures contracts were added. Although several types of bonds were launched, the prices were relatively firm, but still with alternating rises and falls. On Wednesday, the August futures contracts were settled, and the market was closed for the day. The settlement amount was over 31 million, which was quite smooth. On Thursday, prices initially fell due to the rampant communist bandits, but then rebounded due to Finance Minister Song's speech, resulting in a slight improvement of 0.2-0.3 yuan. On Friday, the market weakened again. Due to buying of the 41 bonds, prices initially improved slightly but eventually declined again by 0.2-0.3 yuan. On Saturday, there were rumors of restructuring of the 96 bonds, and the prices of various bonds rose slightly by 0.1-0.2 yuan following the 96 bonds, but the 96 bonds only rose by 0.3 yuan.
