Wireless Weekly

A Discussion on New and Old Medicine 224

— Tianyi

(Reprinted from the Dagongbao Medical Weekly)

Recently, various newspapers have frequently discussed new and old medicine. At first glance, it seems like making a mountain out of a molehill; upon closer consideration, it concerns the rise and fall of science and the strength or weakness of the nation, so we cannot remain silent.

Before discussing this issue, let us first talk about the evolution of the wheel. The handcart was the beginning of the carriage, but the carriage is not comparable to the handcart. In recent years, the inventions of trains, automobiles, and trams are vastly different from carriages, let alone comparable to handcarts. If you were to ask a passerby, which is better for heavy loads and long distances, convenience and easy access, a train or a cart? I dare say they would undoubtedly answer a train. Why is medicine any different? Before the Zhou and Qin dynasties, only acupuncture and moxibustion were mentioned. At the end of the Han dynasty, herbal medicine began to rise. During the Tang dynasty, Buddhist medicine was introduced. In the Song dynasty, it was mixed with Neo-Confucianism. The four masters of the Jin and Yuan dynasties were prosperous for a time, but gradually declined in the Ming and Qing dynasties. In recent centuries, new medicine began to enter China. Therefore, the records of the Inner Canon and Treatise on Febrile Diseases, compared with today's new medicine, are no different from handcarts and carriages. Is it necessary to wait and think before making a judgment?

Some argue that old medicine has inherited thousands of years of tradition and must have its value. They do not know that the reason it has survived to this day is that no better medicine has been introduced to replace it. If handcarts had no carriages or other vehicles invented, their continued use would be unquestionable. Similarly, if the New World had not been discovered and inhabited by Europeans, it would still belong to black people, and their entrenched habits would still be ancient and unchanged. Everything must be compared to determine superiority or inferiority. If superiority and inferiority are distinguished, the superior will survive. Whether medicine stands in society, whether new or old, cannot escape this natural law of evolution.

Most Chinese people hold ancient prejudices and are full of xenophobic ideas. This is a characteristic of our nation inherited for thousands of years. Therefore, there is nothing surprising about the current opposition to new medicine. Here are some historical materials from the Ming and Qing dynasties. I wonder what readers will think!

(1) In the late Ming dynasty, due to the discovery of errors in the Datong calendar, in the late Wanli period, Matteo Ricci, Viegode Pangja, Sabatthirusde Ursis and other foreigners were tasked with revising the calendar. Xu Yuanhu, Li Liang'an and others supported them. At that time, the conflict between new and old was very fierce, most notably Wei Wenkui and Leng Shouzhong. During the Qing dynasty, during the Shunzhi and Kangxi periods, the German Johann Adam Schall von Bell was in charge of the Qin Tian Jian (Imperial Astronomical Bureau). Yang Guangxian and others vehemently criticized the new method, spare no effort. He wrote a book called "Bu De Yi Shu" (Book of Necessity). Later, Yang replaced Tang and took his position. Soon after, he was dismissed for inaccurate calculations, and the controversy subsided.

(2) In the fourth year of the Tongzhi reign in the Qing dynasty, the Englishman Durand built a railway outside Xuanwumen in Beijing, but it was ordered to be demolished due to public opposition. In the thirteenth year, the British company Ewo built the Songhu Railway, but it was eventually bought back and destroyed due to opposition from Feng Jun'guang and Shen Baozhen. In the sixth year of the Guangxu reign, Li Hongzhang requested the construction of the Tangxu Railway. Before the trains had run for long, officials repeatedly impeached him, and after much difficulty, it was finally opened to traffic. At that time, the opponents used the reasons that it was making trouble out of nothing, disturbing the imperial tombs, and that the black smoke emitted was harmful to crops. This remains a point of discussion today.

From this, we can see that in the dispute between new and old, what is right for them is also wrong, and what is wrong for them is also right. The new develops step by step, and the old struggles to survive. This is inevitable and natural. When things change, the superior wins and the inferior loses. The evolutionary pattern is unavoidable, it is certain to happen. What the structure and form of handcarts and carriages are like, I am afraid that few people in this world know.

However, we must give some sincere advice to new medical students, that is, do not fail to live up to your important mission of relieving suffering and strengthening the nation. When Matteo Ricci and others were introduced during the Ming dynasty, how precise was their knowledge of calendrical calculations, but without the promotion and development of Xu and Li, their achievements might not have been so great. Xu Guangqi wrote "Gougu Yi" (The Meaning of Right-Angled Triangles), and Liang'an wrote "Tongwen Suanzhi Huangu Rongjiao Yi" (The Mathematical Canon in Nine Sections), making considerable inventions in calendrical calculations, not just following blindly. Moreover, Guangqi said that to surpass, one must understand everything. Today, the number of people in our country who study new medicine is gradually increasing. How many of them can understand everything? How many can surpass? Following the instructions of the book, I wonder if it can avoid disappointment.

Moreover, it has been heard that there are still some people in new medicine whose knowledge is insufficient, who are at a loss when they see diseases, or who demand money for treatment, acting like wandering quacks, or who do not pay attention to their behavior, causing people to criticize them. Although these are few, they are all obstacles to the development of new medicine. Therefore, we hope that those who are engaged in this profession will recognize the nobility of their profession and the importance of their responsibility, study academic knowledge thoroughly, seek to understand everything in order to surpass, cultivate personal morality, care about people's opinions and protect their position, be sincere in their hearts and manifest it externally, let their virtue increase daily, and achieve remarkable results. So that those who know will be convinced, and even those who used to criticize new medicine will no longer be able to hold different opinions due to the consensus of the public. From then on, new medical knowledge will be practiced throughout the country, so that the mysterious and boring old theories, like handcarts and carriages, will disappear from the world. Wouldn't that be the great fortune of our nation? New medical students, do you think my words are right? I feel compelled to speak so sincerely because of my deep love. It is also a strike of the morning bell.

A Discussion on Jiao Yitang's "Letter to the Nation on the Adoption of National Medicine Regulations" (Continued) 225

— Yu Yunxiu

Mr. Jiao said: "In addition, cold should be treated with heat, and heat should be treated with cold. Although the Inner Canon also says this, national doctors are not rigid about it. Unexpectedly, Western doctors got it right. We know that the high fever phenomenon of general febrile diseases is often a reaction to the toxins of physiological functions. It is appropriate to fully exert their effects. Western doctors actually use ice packs to disperse them, and the phenomenon of high fever clearly decreases, but life is also in danger." I think this statement needs further discussion. Mr. Jiao's reason that "the reaction of physiological function of mildew" is not found in your national doctors' books. Of course, this is the word of scientific medicine. Mr. Jiao knows this reason, wouldn't the Western doctors who use ice packs know it? Since they know this reason, they will come to use ice packs. Of course, at that time, there are more appropriate conditions for the disease than this reason, and then it is necessary to use ice packs. Let me tell Mr. Jiao a rough idea: First, if the high fever lasts for a long time, the brain will be damaged! The locals call it "thermal obstruction", especially for children and the elderly, they cannot withstand high fever. Second, during high fever, the heart works very vigorously. If it is too vigorous, it will be tired and weak! Therefore, when we encounter patients with long-term high fever, we must consider the patient's brain and heart, and must not allow the side effects caused by high fever to increase the disease and lose their lives. However, the simplest, most effective, most harmless, and most controllable method for dealing with high fever and regulating high fever is the ice pack. The national psychology is most afraid of wind and cold, but they don't know the awesomeness of heat. In summer, when they suffer from fever, the air temperature is as high as 36 or 37 degrees Celsius, and the patient's body temperature is as high as 40 degrees Celsius. At that time, they still have to follow the nonsense that "wind is the leader of all diseases", closing the windows tightly and not allowing air to circulate, steaming the patient into a coma, and still not letting go. We often encounter this kind of erroneous custom and uneducated behavior in society. Teaching them to open windows and circulate air is already shocking. If they are taught to use ice, wouldn't they be scared to death? This is really a case of "summer insects cannot talk about ice." Unexpectedly, Mr. Jiao also holds this view and makes this statement. It seems that the discussion of academic principles is too rigid and lacks understanding?

Mr. Jiao wanted to attack our ice packs, and he was afraid that we would use the words of the Inner Canon "cold should be treated with heat, and heat should be treated with cold" to refute him. So he used the slippery words "national doctors are not rigid about it" to lightly cover it up. Alas! Mr. Jiao is too clever. From the perspective of academic principles, rigidity has the academic principles of rigidity, and non-rigidity has the academic principles of non-rigidity. When should one be rigid, and when should one not be rigid, must be based on academic principles. Those national doctors who are uncivilized, have no good equipment, and are not good at diagnosis, are simply blind people riding blind horses, bumping around. They don't even deserve the word "rigidity". What is the possibility of "non-rigidity"? Please stop deceiving the people with words that go beyond the track of academic principles!

Mr. Jiao said: "Secondly, the poverty of medicine, knowing what disease it is, but not knowing what medicine to use, because there are many medicines that Western doctors don't have at all. They have to wait for foreign countries to invent them. The sooner foreign countries invent them, the sooner they can use them. The later foreign countries invent them, the longer they have to wait to use them. If foreign countries never invent them in their lifetime, they can only look at the patient and hope for the best. The most common examples are typhoid fever, tuberculosis, and leprosy. How can there be a specific medicine for any of them? Especially for leprosy, they are isolated and live apart. There is no way to do anything except wait for death." Scientific doctors should accept this accusation! Because the position of scientific doctors is scientific research, and it is the mission of invention, but Mr. Jiao, listen, people of the country! What is research, what is invention? The special characteristic of barbaric and semi-civilized peoples is to regard research and invention as very easy. Mr. Jiao, listen, people of the country! Research and invention are not vague and casual things. They require research places, research time, and research capital. The country and society do not know how to promote true learning, and they do not know how to support true scholars, so that a group of scholars with research skills, research literacy, and research skills are idle in society and are busy with food and clothing. How can they have the time and money to do research? As for schools, if the person who is the principal is not slippery and does not think of other methods, and runs the school seriously by relying on the education fees from the government, I am afraid that even the professors' salaries will be owed, and they still want to establish research rooms and allocate research funds? Unless they disregard the name of the national school, do not support the central stage, and indiscriminately donate money from foreign consortia and enclose land, they can still operate a little. Otherwise, there is simply no way to implement it. Under this situation, what research and invention can be talked about? The personnel of the government should deeply apologize to the academic institutions and to the domestic experts, then they will be considered to have a conscience. It's strange and ridiculous that Mr. Jiao, who has been an official for many years, turned around and declared to the people of the country, accusing us of not researching and not inventing. Mr. Jiao, research and invention are things that come at a price. You can't get something for nothing. Is it that your national doctors say that stroke is fire in the theory of Hejian, and Dongyuan will say that it is qi, and Danxi will say that it is phlegm, and talking about soldiers on paper can be regarded as research and invention? Scientists are not allowed to play tricks and do not want to talk empty words. It is not that they are afraid of hiding it from the people of the country, but that they are afraid of laughing at the world and ridiculing those who know, leaving a stain on the academic circles of our country!

Furthermore, domestic experts have already published considerable achievements in small research and small inventions, but Mr. Jiao just doesn't see them. But Mr. Jiao wants to blame all the difficult-to-treat diseases on modern medical scientists to invent specific medicines. Otherwise, he says that they are just looking at the patients and that there is no way to do anything. This point is too unreasonable. Looking back at your national doctors, what methods do they actually do for the patients? I would like to ask, how far has the invention of specific medicines gone? I would like to ask, don't be busy! Mr. Jiao also has a wonderful passage below praising the richness of national doctors' medicines. I originally wanted to bring up his intention here, so that the readers of the country can compare the two, because I am afraid that it will disrupt the order of Mr. Jiao's original book, so I will put it aside for now and discuss it later.

Common Sense Q&A About Diseases 226

— Cheng Hanzhang

(17) Typhus

(Q) What is typhus?

(A) It is an acute infectious disease with a certain fever pattern, and at the same time, red rashes appear on the skin, and mucositis also occurs in the respiratory tract.

(Q) What is the Western name for typhus?

(A) The Latin is Typhus exanthematicus or Febris exanthematicus or Typhus petecbilis, the German is Flecktyphus or Fleckfieber, the French is Typhus exanthematicue, but the English simply call it Typhus fever or Petechial fever.

(Q) What is the pathogen of this disease?

(A) It is said to be a small body called Rickettsia prowazek, found in the intestines of lice.

(Q) What is the epidemic status of typhus?

(A) This is the most easily infected disease, more prevalent in winter; it occurs a lot in unsanitary places, such as slums, prisons, battlefields, etc. Therefore, it has other names such as famine typhus, prison typhus, or war typhus. The vector is lice.

(Q) Can it not recur after one infection?

(A) After suffering from this disease once, one can be immune for life.

(Q) How many days does it take to develop the disease after being infected with the virus?

(A) It takes one or two weeks of incubation before the disease develops.

(Q) What are the symptoms at the time of onset?

(A) It can be divided into the prodromal stage, the rash stage, and the recovery stage.

Page 18

three phases.

(Q) What are the symptoms of the prodromal stage?

(A) The patient first feels a sudden chill and shivering, and then develops a fever, with the temperature about 39 to 40 degrees Celsius. There is nausea, vomiting, headache, sacral and limb pain, etc. The face is flushed, edematous or expressionless. The pulse is frequent, often leading to insomnia. On the third or fourth day of onset, the dullness boundary of the liver increases, and bronchial catarrh occurs. In addition, there are dizziness, blurred vision, flashes of light, tinnitus, nerve deafness, speech disorders, loss of consciousness, delirium, etc.

(Q) What are the symptoms of the rash stage?

(A) Four to six days after the onset of the disease, the rash is like the size of a pinhead to mung bean, round, light red rose rash. Generally, it starts from the chest and abdomen and spreads all over the body in one or two days, often reaching hundreds. The difference from typhoid fever rash is that the palms and soles of the feet also appear. And there is no recurrence. The rash is congested, but mostly turns hemorrhagic after two or three days, and does not disappear even when pressure is applied.

(Q) What is the state of the fever?

(A) The patient has a persistent high fever, which is remitting. Usually, by the second week, the fever dissipates component by component.

(Q) Does the patient have any other dangerous symptoms?

(A) Sometimes, because of weakness, neurological symptoms are very obvious. There is motor restlessness, hallucinations, fantasies, delirium, high insomnia, lethargy, etc. There may also be urinary retention or fecal incontinence.

(Q) What is the recovery period like?

(A) Two or three weeks after the onset of the disease, the recovery period begins. At that time, various symptoms disappear, and the rash fades, with bran-like desquamation. But sometimes bedsores, gangrene, lower limb neuralgia, and peripheral nerve paralysis occur.

(Q) How dangerous is typhus?

(A) It depends on the condition of the circulatory and nervous systems. It is more serious in the elderly and obese; lighter in children. The mortality rate is 20%.

(Q) Is there an absolute cure for this disease?

(A) Not yet. But injections of simple horse serum, serum from recovering patients, sterilized milk, mercury preparations, or nucleoproteins can be used; the effect is uncertain. Usually, for neurological symptoms, sedatives such as potassium bromide, Medinelevipan, etc. are used. For patients with high fever, ice packs are applied to the head, or several antipyretics are taken internally.

A Bird's-Eye View of Medicine and Pharmacy in Shanghai in the Last Ten Years (Continued) 227

— Pang Shuzhou

Chapter 6 Medical and Pharmaceutical Education and Publications

Section 1 New Medical and Pharmaceutical Education

In addition, Shanghai also has the private Nanyang Medical University and the private Sino-German Women's Medical School. They have been closed down one after another in the past ten years. Nanyang Medical University has several classes of graduates. The Sino-German Women's Medical School closed down shortly after its establishment. So there are no graduates. Most of its students merged into Tongde Medical College. As for those run by foreigners, there is still Harvard Medical School fifteen years ago, located on the current Haig Road. It was later closed. Most of the students studied at Harvard in the United States. These are not very relevant to this article, so I will not elaborate on them.

Looking at the statistics above, the first thing that makes us realize is that there are only more than 1,000 medical students in the whole of Shanghai. It takes 104 full-time teachers and as many as 62 part-time teachers. This is a very uneconomical thing and is also the result of the lack of unification of medical affairs. The second thing that shocks us is that the so-called national schools do not have completely independent affiliated hospitals. And many schools are run by foreigners. Third, although there are several private medical schools run by Chinese people, due to economic difficulties, the hospitals are not perfect. And instead, a small number of teachers lead a large number of students to practice. No one is there to assist with remote learning. If this continues, will there be corruption? Fourth, the National Shanghai Medical College, which has the fewest students, and the Women's Medical College established by the church have the most teachers. On average, the ratio is 90 and 68. Almost one teacher only teaches one and a half students. Isn't this a very thought-provoking thing? Based on the above four points, I think that medical and pharmaceutical education in Shanghai is still somewhat inconsistent with the national conditions of China and is showing a deformed state. Therefore, I associate it with "Jiao Yitang's Letter to the Nation on the Adoption of National Medicine Regulations", which criticized the Ministry of Health for spending huge amounts of money without making any achievements. Perhaps it is making one-sided observations from the deformed health administration and issuing attacks. However, to use this to obliterate science and promote Xuan medicine can be described as throwing the baby out with the bathwater and being completely confused.

In addition to medical and pharmaceutical schools, there are also midwifery schools, which can be said to be the most in Shanghai. There are currently eight:

Sino-German Obstetrics School 126 students

Tongde Obstetrics School 111 students

Dade Obstetrics School About 50 students

Huisheng Midwifery School About 70 students

Renhe Obstetrics School About 80 students

Cihang Midwifery School About 60 students

Baosheng Midwifery School The number of students is unknown at the beginning of this semester

Shengsheng Midwifery School The number of students is unknown at the beginning of this semester

There are three schools that have been closed down: 1) Dahua Obstetrics School 2) Jianhua Obstetrics School 3) Bateli Obstetrics School

All the above-mentioned obstetrics schools only recruit female students and train midwives to deliver babies. The length of study is only two years. The qualification for admission is only junior high school graduation. The school's equipment is stipulated by the Education Bureau and is not very troublesome. With Shanghai's talents, it is of course not difficult to find teachers for some obstetrics schools. With Shanghai's population, it is of course also easy to absorb some ordinary women as teaching materials. Therefore, in the past ten years, this kind of school has sprung up one after another like mushrooms after the rain. According to the above eight schools, an average of 300 graduates can be produced every year. This is originally a good phenomenon. And people in the society have more faith in the new method of delivery than in other medicines. Therefore, it is very optimistic to promote the new midwifery method and abolish the old midwives in a few years. It is only a pity that there are not many midwifery schools in the interior. Small counties and remote areas are lacking. And these schools are all gathered in the prosperous city of Shanghai, which has a slight drawback. Because female students from all over the country come to Shanghai and receive this kind of specialized education, their own lives are often urbanized first, and they are not very willing to return to the countryside to carry out their business. As a result, there is an oversupply of midwives in Shanghai and many of them become female nurses. The interior still feels the lack. A few years ago, I wrote an article in the North China Medical Report, discussing in detail the inappropriateness of establishing obstetrics schools in the largest cities. I didn't expect that there are more large cities now, and the interior is still unable to develop. There are many social problems and the relationship in the current situation. It is not convenient to discuss it more at this time.

The True Meaning of Pharmacy Business (3) 228

— People

Regarding the different natures of pharmacy businesses, in various European countries, they can be distinguished into two types: one is a specialized professional shop, and the other is a general trading shop. The former is referred to as a formal pharmacy in this article, and the latter as an ordinary drug store. Moreover, several countries can differentiate the business nature of pharmacies by their names. For example, in Italy, a formal pharmacy is called "Farmacia," and an ordinary drug store is called "Drogueria." Similar distinctions exist in Germany and France. Unlike our country, which collectively calls them "Dispensary," or the United States, which simply calls them "Pharmacy," Japan also has a system similar to Europe. Formal ones are called [Place Name] Pharmacy, and ordinary ones are called [Place Name] Store. The reason for distinguishing their names is to indicate the different types of business, making it easier for the government to manage, and for pharmacists to understand their responsibilities, avoiding confusion in business operations.

Pharmacy Business in Italy

The pharmaceutical system in Rome is the same as in Spain and Portugal. Formal pharmacies can sell all kinds of medicines and poisons, as well as prescriptions, and handle analysis and microscopy work. Ordinary drug stores are only allowed to sell household medicines and ordinary goods. The state enforces pharmacy laws strictly, and the number of pharmacies is also fixed. The capital city has 250 pharmacies, while there is no such limit for ordinary drug stores. Recently, the number of formal pharmacies has reached its limit, so pharmacists who want to operate in this field can only purchase existing ones from others. Ordinary drug stores are not regulated by law, but thanks to the support of the people, there are no malpractices. The effect they achieve is the same as that of formal pharmacies, except that formal pharmacies can sell all kinds of poisons and prescriptions, and handle analysis and other work. Ordinary drug stores do not have this specialized work and only sell goods, which is very different. Therefore, the boundaries between these two types of business are clear, and there is no risk of confusion.

As the tasks of formal pharmacies are as described above, it goes without saying that they have considerable connections with the medical community. Therefore, the harmony between the medical and pharmaceutical professions in Italy is a commendable point. Some pharmacists even set up waiting rooms for patients. Because customers come to the pharmacy to wait for a doctor's diagnosis and prescription, and then have the medicine dispensed on the spot, doctors can also use the pharmacist's laboratory for testing, which facilitates rapid diagnosis and is very convenient. In fact, a pharmacy is a clinic, or it can be called a pharmacy clinic. Therefore, doctors in Italy do not dispense medicine themselves, which means they do not encroach on other people's businesses. The harmony between medicine and pharmacy is due to professional ethics. However, medical and pharmaceutical professionals have no feelings for ordinary drug store owners, because they lack sufficient knowledge and are ultimately dismissed as outsiders.

Pharmacy Business in Germany

Formal pharmacies in Germany are called Apotheke, and they are limited. The quota depends on the region and the ratio of residents, ranging from one per 6,000 to one per 10,000. Ordinary drug stores are not allowed to sell poisons or prescriptions. The implementation of pharmacy laws is very strict. After completing the pharmacist qualification, one must undergo a two-year apprenticeship in a formal pharmacy before obtaining a license to practice in Germany, which means having the qualification to practice independently. According to German regulations, formal pharmacies are limited and cannot be opened unless through replacement or special permission. To apply for special permission, one must have all the necessary conditions and sufficient capital. Therefore, it is rare for those under the age of 50 to be granted special permission. (To be continued)

Jottings After a Diagnosis 229

— Chen Fangzhi

The Harm of Seeking Perfection

One day, I was at home in Ningbo when I received a phone call from a friend and relative, Mr. So-and-so. He said, "There is a Mrs. Lu who is seriously ill. She has been in a major hospital for two months. It is said that her lungs are damaged, her heart is damaged, her peritoneum is damaged, and her stomach and intestines are damaged. It is so bad that there is no cure. They want to ask you to assess the situation. What do you think?" I said, "I know Mrs. Lu. She has many children. If she is suffering, I sympathize with her very much. Of course, I can go and see her. But since she has been in a major hospital, what is the diagnosis from that hospital?" He said, "Probably tuberculosis and peritonitis." I said, "What are her subjective symptoms? Does she cough? Does she have a fever?" He said, "She has a fever, but not much of a cough. It was said that she had swelling and a large abdomen, but that is better now. She has some pain when urinating, and her menstruation comes often and lasts a long time, even every two weeks. This symptom has been going on for four months." I said, "In that case, she has a gynecological problem. She should also see a gynecologist. And please have her send a urine sample for testing as a reference for the diagnosis." He said, "I will send the urine sample, and please invite a gynecologist on our behalf."

After we received their urine sample and tested it, there was only a trace of protein and many pus cells and epithelial cells. Based on the urine, it was entirely evidence of cystitis, nothing else. So, I and a gynecologist friend went to Mrs. Lu's residence. First, we examined her in detail within the scope of internal medicine. Her lungs, except for a slight hardening of the percussion sound at the apex of the left lung, were otherwise normal. The so-called tuberculosis was completely wrong. The slight hardening at the apex of her left lung may have been an old, past tuberculous lesion, but there was no active tuberculosis. Her heart had no murmurs, but her heartbeat was accelerated, and her pulse was accelerated (126 beats per minute), which were both symptoms of systemic weakness.

The question was, where did this systemic weakness come from? Examining her abdomen, the abdominal wall was soft as usual, with no swelling or ascites. When asked why there was talk of swelling, they said, "She had swelling before, and it was tense and painful when it was swollen. She couldn't even pass gas, and it made a booming sound when tapped." Ah! I understood. It turned out that the swelling was caused by the onset of cystitis and was mistaken for peritonitis. Ah! That was it. Examining her abdomen again, the liver, spleen, kidneys, etc., were normal, with no swelling. Only the lower abdomen was slightly tender, which was due to cystitis.

In short, the patient they claimed had damaged lungs, heart, peritoneum, and intestines was, unexpectedly, found by an unskilled person like myself to have none of those damages. However, there was evidence of heart weakness, which came from systemic weakness. I deduced that she had cachexia and suspected a uterine disease. So, I asked the gynecologist to examine her with a hysteroscope. As expected, she had uterine cancer. Then, everything was clear. I asked her if the major hospital had examined her uterus. She said they had not. Ah! That was it.

I thought that we had diagnosed her condition, making her confused illness clear, and that should be considered a merit. Unexpectedly, trouble arose in this clarity. It would have been fine if people had continued to say that her internal organs were all diseased. Now that I, a busybody, had found out that she had uterine cancer, I had become troublesome. The patient's family said, "What can be done about uterine cancer?" We said, "The time for treatment has been missed, and surgery is no longer possible." The patient's family said, "Then, is there any other good method?" We said, "We can try radiation with radium needles, but unfortunately, there is none in Ningbo." The patient's family said, "Is there any in Shanghai?" We said, "Of course, there is." The patient's family said, "Can we go to Shanghai for radiation?" We said, "At this stage, we cannot guarantee how effective radiation will be, but you can still go." The patient's family said, "Is there any danger on the way?" I said, "Ningbo to Shanghai is only one night's journey. I can guarantee that." Our consultation ended there. Later, they went to Shanghai. I don't know what hospital they went to, what doctor they saw, what the doctor said, or if they had radiation. I heard that she died after more than ten days! The cachexia of cancer is, of course, a deadly disease. Death is not surprising. In my opinion, Mrs. Lu's death had made the cause of her death clear, unlike most people who die in a confused state.

Later, I heard from many friends that everyone in the patient's family, except for her who could no longer speak, said that I was bad. First, my medical skills were bad, because the doctors in Shanghai also said that her heart, liver, spleen, lungs, and kidneys were all damaged, which was consistent with the major hospital. This showed that Chen Fangzhi was wrong. Second, my conscience was bad, saying that I knew the patient was going to die, but deliberately sent her to Shanghai to die. There were all kinds of nonsense, and I couldn't care less.

Free Talk

Biographical Literature 230

— Yu Dafu

Chinese biographical literature, since Sima Qian and up to the present, has generally been dominated by the old-fashioned style of sequential biographies. As for variations, there are tomb inscriptions, elegies, and accounts written by descendants to glorify their ancestors, so-called flattering tomb writings, which are perhaps somewhat similar. But these are always monotonous, and everyone, after death, is invariably a perfect person with complete wisdom, benevolence, and courage. I have never seen a vivid piece of writing that can portray a person's weaknesses and shortcomings. However, "Water Margin" is also called biography, and literary critics regard it as a collective biography of 108 people. "The True Story of Ah Q" also exists, and Ah Q is the most well-known one among the new literature that has been popular for more than a decade. If we regard such literature as biography, then Sun Wukong's "Journey to the West" and Dong Xiaowan's "Memories" are also biographies. The scope of biographical literature that I am talking about is definitely not that broad.

So, what kind of biographical literature is lacking in China? Precisely because China lacks these, even one example cannot be found. If we look for materials in foreign literature, there are indeed many immortal biographical works. A slightly older era and a style somewhat similar to "Records of the Grand Historian," but with completely different content, is Plutarch's "Parallel Lives of the Noble Greeks and Romans." A more recent era, which describes the words, deeds, thoughts, personality, and surroundings of a person's life in great detail, is James Boswell's "Life of Johnson." With an elegant style, fresh writing, and indirect approaches, to narrate a person's life in a very interesting way, there is Lytton Strachey's "Queen Victoria," André Maurois' "Ariel," and Pierre Courthion's "Portraits de Seurat." In addition, there are lively biographies written by the German Emil Ludwig, the Italian Giovanni Papini, and others, which are too many to mention. Precisely because China lacks this kind of biographical writer, only self-praising autobiographies and derivative critical biographies are popular in the market. But from the fact that a great man like Sun Yat-sen is still offering rewards to solicit biographies in newspapers, it can be imagined that the biographical literature in China is declining.

On Courtliness 231

— Xu Maoyong

Henri Barbusse, the French literary giant who is said to be coming to China but has not yet arrived, specifically stated when using the term "intellectual class" in a small book:

"Intellectual class丨I use this to refer to people who think, not to people who are witty, boastful, sycophantic, or exploit others spiritually."

"Witty people" means those who are good at being courtly. Courtliness, boasting, sycophancy, and spiritual exploitation: these four are all so-called "art of the clown." But technically, the first and fourth types are much more difficult. When used well, success is easier; when used poorly, it is also easier to run into a wall. Moreover, the status of these two types of artists is much higher than that of boasters and sycophants, because boasting and sycophancy are clearly the work of a snobbish servant. But a courtly person and a spiritual exploiter are quite like a gentleman, who is called a "guest" under the master.

I will now only talk about courtliness.

To choose a typical example from courtly people, I think it is best to choose Yang Xiu, the "child Yang Dezu" who was even admired by Mi Heng. Literary tradition says that he "had talent and learning," and "A New Account of the Tales of the World" praises his "quick wit." But in reality, his talent and learning, his quick wit, were only used as a drinking game for Cao Cao. His lifelong effort was in courtliness. When Cao Cao wrote the character "活" (live) on his "Prime Minister's Gate," he immediately ordered people to tear down the gate and rebuild it, because he knew that "the prince was just complaining that the gate was too big." When Cao Cao wrote the character "合" (together) on a box of food, he immediately ate it, because he knew that "the duke was teaching people to take a bite." In addition, there are the stories of "excellent words" and "bamboo shields," which are the most outstanding deeds in Yang Xiu's life. At that time, even Cao Cao sighed, "My talent is not as good as yours." Others, of course, "admired his eloquence," because they were not as good at being courtly.

However, in the last act of courtliness, he ran into a wall and lost his life. In the "chicken ribs" incident, many people called for justice for Yang Xiu. In fact, Cao Cao's idea was correct, because courtliness is only suitable for peacetime. If one interferes with courtliness in military and national affairs, it is unavoidable to cause mistakes. In this respect, Cao Cao trusted Dian Wei and Xu Chu. But Cao Cao killed Yang Xiu, so his tyranny was indeed a great mask.

Today, the situation of courtliness has changed greatly. First, now it is necessary to be courtly not only to individuals, but also to groups. Second, due to material convenience, those who are courtly do not have to do so in front of the master. As long as they publish some writings in newspapers and magazines, there is hope of being appreciated.

However, no matter what era they live in, masters are happy to have someone be courtly, but in practice, they still trust another kind of person.

Tracing back to ancient times, did not Lord Mengchang, who had three thousand retainers, later realize that "menial skills like crowing and stealing" were more practical?

From this point of view, the fortune of courtly people seems to have never been very prosperous.

According to my thinking, the reason for this lack of prosperity is, first, that they only know how to be courtly; second, that they want to maintain their status too much, and are not as straightforward as sycophants and boasters, thus making the master feel that their pretentiousness is unbearable.

There is also this story in "A New Account of the Tales of the World":

"Fan Xuanping was a man who liked to use intelligence and calculation, but sometimes he lost due to excessive calculation. Once, he lost his official position and lived in Dongyang. Grand Marshal Huan was in Nanzhou, so he went to seek refuge with him. Huan was trying to recruit dissidents to undermine the court, and Xuanping was also known in the capital, so Huan thought that he had come from afar to join him, and he was very happy… Although Fan was actually seeking refuge with Huan, he feared that it would damage his reputation, so he said, 'Although I have the intention of paying tribute to the court, my lost son is being treated here, so I came to visit my relatives.' Huan was disappointed, and his expectation disappeared."

This kind of pretense is the essence of the art of the clown. Unfortunately, Huan Wen was also a great mask (although I have never seen him on stage, I assume so), so he disdained him, causing Mr. Fan to fail.

Originally, the art of the clown is only for dressing up clowns as young masters.

Xue Juexing (Continued) 232

— Ba Jin

If we admit that drama is a kind of public education, then we can see what kind of spiritual nourishment the Chinese people often receive. These things grab them, make them go backwards day by day, and do not let them move forward a step. However, those higher gentlemen who eat with "culture", in addition to promoting the national drama, also sent actors who played women overseas, cheated a signboard abroad, and deceived the people. They said that they used this "culture" to spiritually conquer foreign countries.

The pink curtain on the stage fell for the last time that night. The audience scrambled to go out. Many people crowded at the door, and the situation looked chaotic. It was more difficult to pass through that door. After a series of collisions between flesh, my two friends and I finally went downstairs, out of the theater, and stood on the embankment.

The time was past twelve o'clock. That friend also asked me to go to a small shop to eat something, but my tiredness made me decline. I said goodbye to them, and I walked alone on the embankment, walking through the encirclement of rickshaws, and slowly walked towards Haizhu Bridge.

My heart was lonely. Many melancholy thoughts surrounded me. Before my eyes was a piece of darkness, without light, without a future, and all were only some ghosts. A strong hatred burned in my heart. I cursed all the old dramas in China. I cursed all the old legacy of China. I cursed the entire Eastern culture. I asked in despair: Is there really anyone who cares about the future of the Chinese nation now? (I believe there must be) Why is no one seen coming out to severely attack the so-called Eastern culture that truly poisons the Chinese nation? (I believe there must be) Why does no one know that the deformed monsters that now fill China are all products of the so-called Eastern culture, and their thoughts and behaviors are all similar to those ghosts? (I believe there must be.)

"Siku Quanshu" is a treasure, the antiques of the Forbidden City are treasures, Buddhist temples are treasures, historical sites are treasures... Everything that can leave a shadow in the minds of the nation struggling on this road to the new are treasures of the ruling class! Many people believe this. However, in fact, without these things, the Chinese people can live a better life. Why should modern people know the ghost tricks of the old times? Humans do not live by history. Although history tells people not to do something, the result is that it tells people to imitate. At least half of the people visiting the Palace of Versailles want to be Louis XIV. People who visit the Forbidden City will have a strange ghost-like thought at that moment.

We need to forget everything and move forward on the new road with a new force. This is our only way out. However, others grab our souls with all kinds of antiques and make us forever fall into the abyss of slavery. It is not surprising that higher gentlemen promote old dramas. Now even some people who originally have nothing to do with pen and ink know to promote reading the classics. Thinking about the future of the Chinese nation in this environment, I can't help but feel grief and anger.

My thoughts will probably not be understood by anyone. I remember expressing the above opinion in this year's essay contest about dreams in the "Eastern Magazine". I said that the various antiques contained in the term Eastern culture block my eyes and make me unable to see the future of China. There was a period of time when I even believed that China had no future. This meaning is very clear.

However, many people therefore call me a pessimist. Am I really a pessimist?

Back at the Henan Machine Workers' Union, I breathed a sigh of relief. I am now back in the human world.

Editorial Office 233

Mr. Guobao: Received your letter. According to Mr. Zhao Jingshen's letter: Pearl S. Buck's "The First Wife and Other Stories" was published by John Day Company, New York. Editor

Woman (11) 234

— Shen Congwen

The woman said with her mouth, "It doesn't matter if the boat is broken," but in her heart she was thinking: "There should be a 'small boat' that is more solid and firm than this small boat, to carry this heart and sail into the vast and boundless sea of people!" She looked ahead and saw a small boat of ideals. Strong arms, a strong soul, everything has not yet been soiled by human affairs. As if smiling with satisfaction, she almost instinctively felt everything about their future.

She felt that she was beautiful, and she understood that in the eyes of the person in front of her, she was almost too beautiful. She understood that he had timidly and greedily noticed every part of her body. She was a little shy, but she was not afraid of him, nor was she tired of him.

He had no doubts about her. He was just a freshman in college, and all his interests and views, including his knowledge of women, would not leave the limitations of that grade. He did not read much, had limited understanding of life, and was slowly learning the life of a city person. He would also become a mediocre and unoriginal city person. When she first saw him, he seemed completely unworldly. After talking a few more words, she understood that all the bad things that senior high school had instilled in students, this person had also completely received his due share. But for some strange reason, this man with the atmosphere of a country person, just that bit of wildness and simplicity, made her always feel more interesting than gentlemen. He was not very smart, but the courage of a newborn calf who was not afraid of anything in the world seemed to make him great, even if it did not make him smart. It's true, this child can become great!

She asked him:

"Do you swim in the sea every day?"

He nodded, so she asked again:

"When will you leave this beach?"

"I don't even know myself."

"You should know yourself. Do what you want, don't you think so?"

"It's useless even if I think."

"Is that a child's way of speaking, or an old man's way of speaking? Children believe in their parents because they are controlled by their families, so they can say that. Old people believe in God, because they think that everything has been arranged by God, so they often don't torture their emotions too much. You…"

When the woman said this, she looked at the shy expression next to her, so she stopped talking. She could estimate that he was not an "old man". She smiled.

The man, because someone had mentioned children and old people, as if inviting him to choose for himself, had to say the following words.

"I came with my dad. My dad is a counselor in the XX department. Someone invited us to Laoshan, and I lived on the mountain for two days and got bored, so I ran back alone. Dad is still on the mountain writing poetry!"

"Your dad can write poetry?"

"He's a poet. He and Liang Rengong, Xia XX, have…"

"Ah, are you Mr. XX's son?"

"Do you know my dad?"

"I saw him once when he gave a lecture at XX. I know him, but he doesn't know me."

"Would you like to tell me…"

Talk

Errand Boy General 235

— Xiao Zhi

Lately, I often heard friends say: there is a general shining shoes on Avenue Joffre. At the time, I thought he must be another so-called "Russian" general. What's so strange about that? Because there are many petty thieves and the like on Avenue Joffre who are White Russians, aristocrats from the time of the former Tsar. If they can use a skill like shining shoes for people to make a living, they should truly be considered lucky among the upper echelons. However, I was wrong. This general's surname is Jiang, his given name is Minsheng. He is indeed a general of our great Republic of China, and one who once shed blood to resist the Japanese for the sake of national survival!

Yesterday, in the local news section of this newspaper, there was a news story with a large headline about this shoe-shining general. According to the report: the general, a native of Harbin, was formerly under the command of Ding Chao, an anti-Japanese general in the Northeast. Having drifted to Shanghai, he was given funds by a refugee relief organization to buy shoe polish and brushes to shine shoes for pedestrians on Avenue Joffre, which was enough for him to make a living. Yesterday, he sent a letter to the relief organization and donated five yuan to help Northeast refugees, reporting on his income and expenses and expressing his gratitude.

For a dignified general to squat on the streets and alleys shining shoes for passersby, of course, a bunch of "masters" or so-called "ambitious" tough guys would laugh at him as being lowly and base, humming "Better to die!" But some people are also saying: If he weren't a fool and could have thrown himself into the arms of "Manchukuo," wouldn't he still be a general, second to none, awe-inspiring and full of murderous intent? Of course, some people will sigh and say: For the officers and soldiers who died in the anti-Japanese war, the state has even hired monks and Taoists to chant scriptures to give them a posthumous commendation, but those who survived and were displaced are left to their own devices with no one to care for them, with at most some minor and not widespread assistance from popular organizations! Isn't this treating the dead generously? Perhaps they are afraid that the dead will go to the underworld to file a complaint, thus enraging the King of Hell, and arresting all the enthusiastic anti-Japanese generals and soldiers, and wouldn't it be better to be polite, and instead stir up a big disaster? The most humorous and most painful tone is: Jiang Minsheng is just a character who resisted Japan for the sake of patriotism, fortunately not dying, and even more fortunately having a relief organization and being able to shine shoes for passersby so that he can continue to live, isn't that enough to be satisfied with? Compared with Liu Chongwu and others, who similarly threw grenades to warn unscrupulous merchants for the sake of patriotism and were deemed "breaking the law" and tasted the taste of iron bars, the preferential treatment, grace, and honor are truly incomparable and beyond measure!

However, these things don't seem to be very relevant. The fact that is placed before our faces and stimulates our eyeballs is: Jiang Minsheng is a general who shed blood to fight against imperialists for the survival of the nation-state in the Northeast Volunteer Army, and now he is drifting on this Avenue Joffre in Shanghai, a place of song, dance, revelry, and prosperity, shining shoes for passersby at the alley entrance opposite the "Cathay Theatre," the "most magnificent, majestic, and noble building on the sea"!

Alas, resisting Japan! Alas, officers and soldiers who resisted Japan and did not die on the battlefield!

Peace Donation 236

— Yi Yan

Everywhere you look, you can see that our compatriots love peace, such as the timely donations for the Taiping Gong Jiao (peaceful offering) and the proportional success of our previous anti-Japanese donations or aviation donations, which are good proofs of this.

I remember a month ago, two Boy Scouts came to my alley to solicit aviation donations. Nine out of ten of my esteemed neighbors slammed the door in their faces, and some even muttered: "Little brothers, what are you raising money to buy airplanes for, to fight the Easterners? It's none of our adults' business if China is destroyed, so why should it be the children's concern?" Hey, friends! Don't say they are cold-blooded animals, they are disgusted with war, they want to give alms on the road to peace!

Look! Recently, in our alley, every now and then, some "big shots" would come in to solicit donations for the timely "promoting peace," politely knocking on people's back doors in turn with a donation book in their hands.

"Old lady, please donate some money for the Taiping Gong, to ensure the peace of this alley throughout the four seasons," they said to an old woman who came to open the back door.

"Is it a donation to perform the Taiping Jiao (peaceful offering)? Good, good, I'll donate one yuan," the straightforward, peace-loving old woman replied.

So, one yuan, six jiao, they collected donations in turn, truly, not a single household failed to donate. Don't believe it? Just look at the yellow receipts pasted on the back doors of each house!

A few days later, the alley was indeed filled with lanterns and streamers, and in the evening, a group of civilized performers with brand-new electrical equipment were invited to perform the Jiao. At that time, the alley was filled with harmony and was crowded with people. The elders who mastered the Dharma and Hong skills, after distributing food to the hungry ghosts, even cooperated in singing a Jiangbei Tan Huang (local opera), truly thoughtful! They thought that the hungry ghosts in mid-July hadn't heard opera in a long time, but I saw that the number of people listening to the opera on the scene was at least ten times greater than the number of ghosts listening to the opera. Alas, is this the original intention of the elders' compassion!

The day after the Jiao was performed, a yellow statement of accounts was posted at the entrance of the alley, showing that more than one hundred yuan had been collected, which was used up without a single cent remaining. However, our alley comrades' belief in this account is incomparable to our belief in the accounts published in the newspapers regarding the receipt and disbursement of national salvation donations.

Haha! In the end, our compatriots believe in peace!

— Feng Wenfeng

Ms. Feng Wenfeng's Calligraphy (Brief Biography) 237

Ms. Feng Wenfeng is a native of Heshan, Guangdong. She is skilled in calligraphy, painting, fine embroidery, and also proficient in Kharosthi script. She became famous in South China for her calligraphy and painting ten years ago. She founded the China Women's Calligraphy and Painting School, cultivating hundreds of talented individuals. Her works have been submitted to art exhibitions at home and abroad, winning more than thirty medals. Her calligraphy is steady and purely derived from her father, Shi Han. Shi Han has a fondness for epigraphy and writing clerical script for thirty years. Ms. Feng received personal instruction and deeply explored the origins of the hall. It is fitting that her calligraphy is extraordinary.

Before Dawn 238

— Yi Ping

When I was at home, the thing I hated the most was the early morning, because my house was in a very lively alley along the road with many people, and it was the first house at the entrance of the main alley, so the sounds from the street and the alley went directly into my windows. All day long, even in the middle of the night, various noisy sounds, such as streetcar sounds, hawking sounds, and the noisy sounds of naughty children, continued non-stop, so not only was there no peace during the day, but even at night it was impossible to sleep peacefully. After midnight, at two or three o'clock, the big city was completely silent in the land of sleep, so I could steal a moment of peace and indulge in sweet dreams. But in a flash, it was before dawn. At this time, in addition to the rooster's wake-up call, there was also a sound that I was used to hearing, and it could even be said that I hated it the most, which was the group of coolies pushing wheelbarrows who came every day to break my sweet dream. The rolling sound of the wheels continued non-stop. I vaguely cursed them for being ignorant of the times! But I clung to the quilt and went back to sleep in a daze, waking up three or four hours later. But sometimes I was indeed disturbed by them so that I couldn't sleep, and I opened my eyes wide, looking at the top of the mosquito net, and thought of my four or five years of wandering life, having tasted the bitter cup of life, and I would think of this group of coolies, what were they doing getting up so early? Did they not like to sleep peacefully and come to taste the pressures of heat and cold? "Life," two big characters appeared before my eyes. We sell our brains every day to make a living, they rely on their physical strength, pushing and walking, whether it is a heavy load of ten or a hundred pounds, whether it is a long distance of ten or a hundred miles, selling two strong arms and two thick black legs. Going out at dawn and returning at dusk, working hard for more than ten hours from morning to night, every day, every month, every year, in cold, heat, wind, and rain, for the sake of a daily income of five or six mao, raising the old and caring for the young, and maintaining the life of the family. If they don't work for a day, the whole family will sit and wait to die. They do this kind of animalistic life from lively youth to white-haired old age. All their lives they have no comfortable residence, delicious nutrition, or spiritual or material well-being, and they are oppressed. They are born from suffering and die from suffering, and in the end, they return naked. However, looking back at the capitalists who are well-fed all day long, they rely on the blood and sweat of the workers to enjoy material and spiritual happiness. We are all humans, why is there such a vast difference? Thinking about it, I pitied them because of my own situation. Every day before dawn, when I hear the rolling sound of the wheels, I hope that the world will also have a day of dawn!

Drama

War and Peace (15) (Four-Act Drama) 239

— Ling He

Act Two: A Group of Refugees

Madam: Oh! Are there still a few of you who haven't come?

Concubine: Hmph, yes.

Madam: There are really a lot of people outside, all of them are villagers. I don't know where they all came from.

Concubine: We're fleeing, and they have to flee too.

Madam: Oh, so they're all refugees?

Young Master: De Fa, come over here. (The young master and the orderly walk to the refreshment room.)

Madam: They're really pitiful, all with disheveled hair and dirty faces, ragged and tattered, like a group of beggars.

Young Master: I'm asking you, why did that fat woman run into our room? Isn't this room reserved by us?

Orderly: Yes, I don't know why she ran in here either. When she first came in, it seemed that someone from the railway bureau brought her in. Because the young masters were not here, I didn't dare to make a decision to force her to leave.

Madam: When I walked past them, the smell was really terrible, probably everyone had a lot of lice on them.

Young Master: Then you can tell her that this is reserved by us. Don't you dare say that? Who is she?

Orderly: Then please, young master, negotiate with the stationmaster.

Concubine: Yes, I was just thinking of going outside to take a look, but I couldn't even move my feet. The children were crying and crying, and it was simply deafening.

Young Master: Should I go now? Might as well wait a while.

Madam: It's really too hard to flee like this. But there's no way not to flee, the rumors have been really tight these past few days.

Maid: Madam, if the Japanese soldiers really come, only the common people will suffer.

Madam: Why?

Concubine: Didn't they flee too!

Maid: No, those who have fled now are probably still people who have a bowl of rice to eat. I'm afraid there are still many who can't escape. They don't even have food to eat, so where would they get the travel expenses?

Madam: Stop talking nonsense, what do you know?

(A noisy human voice, from far to near.)

Concubine: (Looking out the window) Oh, there are more and more people, there are no seats over there, they are all crowding over here.

Madam: Hey, Aunt Zhou, I'm really tired, I want to take a nap.

Concubine: Eldest young master, what are you standing there for? Look, they are all crowding over here.

Young Master: Hmph, aren't they? (Also looking out the window)

Concubine: What, is it just you standing there?

Young Master: No, De Fa is also here.

Concubine: Oh? Hee hee hee hee!

Young Master: What are you laughing at?

Concubine: Do you have to ask? How strange.

Young Master: De Fa, go to the station and make a phone call to ask why they haven't come yet. (The orderly unhappily goes out from the right door. The concubine immediately walks to the refreshment room.)

Concubine: How is it? Are you happy that I came?

(The eldest young master opens his arms and waits for her, and the concubine throws herself into her son's arms in a coquettish manner.)

Young Master: Good sister, are you right? We are really grateful that the Japanese soldiers are coming, otherwise, how could we be so affectionate together? This is our honeymoon trip!

Concubine: Hahaha, (laughs loudly, leaves her son's embrace.) You cold-blooded animal, are you willing to be a slave of a fallen country?

Young Master: What slave of a fallen country or not, I haven't thought about these things at all. I just want to stay with you like this, and it's fine no matter what I do.

Concubine: Oh, don't say such nice things, when you marry a wife, I'm afraid you won't even bother with me!
